et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, then scrape them out completely if you can, and those that you cannot have, let it be until the wound putrefies.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it dry up and become closed at the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said, to help heal and close it quickly.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	and if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then treat it in this way that I have said in its chapter, to close the opening and heal the wound.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a cut from a lance or a knife and the wound is deep, see if the patient feels windy or chills, then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep and it's fresh with all its blood, then don't put powder on it at first hour nor tie it up to stop the bleeding that will drain in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and revive the patient, and bring them back to life.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but put on an attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, then put in the wound old cotton to suck out more moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there doesn't come a spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor any sign of decline.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with stitches and other treatments until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it can't heal and suppurate, then know that there is a fistula, and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or a knife and it's simple, or on the buttocks, or on the back, then treat it as one would for wounds in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it's large, by suturing; and if it's small, with powder; and if it's deep in the bone and has cut pieces, then clean the wound, and scrape out any fragments that are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they're not loose, then let the wound putrefy, so that the extractions will come together again.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the purging of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The purging of the belly is great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound that sometimes pierces the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, by which their introduction takes place.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse for a small wound than a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because in such cases one must put the intestines back together with needles, if they are not replaced hot to hot.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they cannot be put back together with needles.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because it is more useful for a medium wound, because one can sew the intestine back to its place with other two needles.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the purging of the belly is in three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common sutured ones happen in the suturing of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the suturing of other wounds on the body, and two other clean stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all the same they are more proper with the stomach's stitch, and I will say each one and declare them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine comes out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if something needs to be put back, it must be done by one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because the wound is small, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	moisten a sponge or one moist cloth in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you heat it in water with mint and cinnamon.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and warm the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and after that it will restrain its blood and be moist so that only a little remains to drain.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, if you moisten the intestine with water or broth and that it is cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this the entrance is closed up to the point of nothing.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small pouch for the wound with the instrument used to cauterize hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is better than the cutting.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut it without great necessity, for there is no need to do so.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut within in a curved shape and not straight outwards, and look at this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine shoots out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in place according to its natural form in its proper location.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	since you cannot do any better, for that is the best way.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so that you make the sick person lie on their back on a bed.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then place the head and breast higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the bruise of the belly is in one of the two sides,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so that your intent is that the injured part be higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to remember what I have said in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	In small wounds, apply that which is prescribed for them.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take in your hands one gentle servant who knows the whole bruise by touch,
et assemble les levres;	and gather up the edges;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common way of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or more, according to the size of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound two or three spaces, and put in a needle where there is good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two ends of the thread.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pass through from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather up the two heads of the thread and tie them four times.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then wrap around the needle from two sides a string of twine or cord.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and then tie up the two heads of the wound in order.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave two or three spaces, and put in another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread just as you tied it for the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this with each needle, according to what you need.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is closed up.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the needles smaller, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those too coarse cannot well enter:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not seem right to push the needles too far out into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they pierce and open up the wound before the stitching.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles, so that they do not prick or harm the sick person while they are sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put threads or cloths on the ends of the needles to keep them secure.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them like that until the wound is closed and stitched.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it suffices to use one needle or two,
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you gather up the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the thread together with one needle where there is a strong medium-sized thread,
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these heads all three together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then turn the needle at the part where you started, in the way that one sews a dress.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave spaces between each stitch the size of a small coin.
ceste costure sevent li home,	This stitching is known to men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that was on the belly of an ox.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been stabbed with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in length,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the entrails were well out two palms in length.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the entrails and they had been out for 24 hours already.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was stitched up just in 15 days, and it healed, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where we could not find any, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I applied to the wound old cotton two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced through the skin straight and true, tie the thread or stitch where you put in the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from the inner part to the outer part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the meaning of this stitch is that you sew just like a tailor does with furs.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave one thread from one side and take it up again from the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Gauls call properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is to assemble the two parts together naturally, just like some people do.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and then apply one of the heads of the thread to the other head, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or the end of the thread nearby, and make it pierce only that part.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	with the two ends of the thread.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, in two other threads of thread that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Gauls say this phrase, and many bear witness to it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one must sew the belly with two needles, or there be thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and you should push one needle from this side and the other from that side, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is more serious than other wounds in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as that of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it's when you find the fresh wound with all its blood still in it, just like the fire has changed.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	it puts back the intestine and the flesh, then puts on the powder of aromatic herbs.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the fire has changed it, he puts on any ointment that is available until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and they cut the thread, and sew together the skin and the flesh.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then he cures the wound just like the others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then put on old cotton as soon as it starts to heal, right away.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and turn it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you don't need any other medicine, even in more severe conditions, as long as the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you suspect that the wound is turning into a community of main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	it is necessary that you bathe lightly with warm tempered oil or rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and apply it around the joints and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if it feels pain or burning in the bowels, and many times has happened,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then clean them with black wine vinegar, and above all if the burning comes just to the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestines called "youn" cannot be healed if they are injured,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the delicate nature of the intestines that they are, and because of their subtlety throughout the entire body, and their approach to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts out of the wound, put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, you should tie the place that is black, so that no bleeding comes from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are intestines and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the stitches,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two ends hanging from under the wound to outside in order to ease the extraction when the intestine bursts and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are swollen and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded with a lance in the belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became gangrenous and turned into an abscess, and there came out pus and gas.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put a dressing on it according to what I knew, and I did not cease to refine it until it was healed, and the place sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sutured, I doubted that the sickness had done harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and the experienced ones said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take from flax to great thickness, then gather the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the flax has overlapped the mouth, put it on the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it tightens its mouth over;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then tie the head so that it stays like that and cannot be untied.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another flax thread behind in this manner as before, until the wound is completely wrapped up;
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This head will secure itself in the intestine and bring no harm to the sick person,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one ties the intestine with a thin thread that is sewn from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread that is somewhat clean-shaven,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread one thread of fine linen twisted.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle and sew the intestine, and bring it through the wound;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing with flax is not unlike the way of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the main intestines, there is no remedy or healing, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be;
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes gangrenous, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise if it bursts open and starts to heal.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the greenish white nodulation which is hard and firm, or where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also burst open like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes bursts out clear and sometimes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes pus, and at other times enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and has no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is only due to one of the eight reasons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or body.
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much discharge;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the place is corrupted and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine used for treatment is not good.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague,
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of its property in the region it delays digestion, and delays healing, and flees by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are intestines or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and remedies for medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary that I tell you about the remedy for fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the thread, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint in the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and it is in such places that it comes to the property of the main member, and appears on the similar place.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of serious healing, and there is no remedy except labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it clearly, take a needle of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, sew it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, search for a very fine thread of linen.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the linen folds smoothly around the twists.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot well search it with threads,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then clean it through one of the openings.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture runs from one opening to another and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then sew it up as well as you can, knowing if there are bones or nerves and if it is burst open in depth.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the sick person well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where it hurts.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you about, then sew according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and cut away the rotten and corrupted flesh that is inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then sew until it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep in the right place, it is necessary that you cut into depth as far as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put damp threads with medicinal juice on them, and insert them just to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine dissolves the remaining excess that is left at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put on ointments with healthy flesh so that it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve bothers or hurts the main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it all away until the corruption is completely removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then sew up with healthy flesh as much as possible so that it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and bursts open again just like before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the end;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it bursts open and sews until you reach the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then repair the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep and you cannot get to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	then there is no other remedy except for the natural dissolution.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can grasp it with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then pull it out with an instrument suitable for that.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then extract them all, without leaving any behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it difficult and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut and remove the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on a dressing to prevent corruption,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the place around the bones becomes rotten.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will be more easily taken out;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as from the thigh or hip,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove the corruption as much as possible until all blackness is removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great corruption and comes just to the bone marrow;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it needs to be cleaned and covered all the way up to the corruption, and then heal until it is closed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula which happened to one man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matter came to the leg and was followed by a large abscess, and he had no other sign outside for it to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but through their foolishness they cut so high that the abscess opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a lot of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and there were many holes that all went to the inside and moist part of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many surgeons put a cure around it for two years, and there was no remedy in their skill as craftsmen,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called to it, and I came to his leg and the remedies with which they were treating him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what was coming out through the holes was of great bulk;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the flesh of the young man became red and had a yellowish-green hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I sewed a tent in one of the holes, and then searched out all the holes,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that each hole was communicating with the others from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes as far as I could until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption was coming right to the bone within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I extracted what appeared from the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except for what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, and it could not be closed;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and uncovered the bone just as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the corruption was continuing in the bone, and I extracted it, and then removed it, and I set my mind to closing the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I couldn't do it until I cut around an inch of bone, and pulled it forward to its full length,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicines, and he was healed and closed quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to re-start the operation except for the weakness of the sick person, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through blood evacuation he often bled, but he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone there grew a hard flesh, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or contraindication from anything at all, either to eat or to take.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be extracted in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a thread or string, and stretch it to the head of the bone which is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another thread of linen, thicker than the first thread, and tie it above the flesh which is over the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head, so that you pull out the corrupted flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the place where you see to extract it, so that the extraction does not cut the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a skewer or a thin board under the bone to move and cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to extract as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and extract again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh, then put a skewer under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then extract from one part to the other the corruption, and make sure that the extractor is long enough for the corruption, just as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and extract the bone where it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of the two joints, then there is no remedy but to cut it out;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the wrist of the foot, then it is very serious.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you must investigate that corrosion, how it opens up;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways that you can, but in such a way that you do not harm the vein or the nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the knives and the extractors for cutting those bones are many, according to the thickness of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their density and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each appearance of the operation.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to your knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways in which diseases manifest themselves;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can perish either from an internal cause or from an external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated the corruption with remedies and it does not improve.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member right up to the place where the corruption comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the sick person escapes either by death, or by a greater evil, which is the defect of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the members become black, so that it seems they have been burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards it spreads after the blackness has appeared, then the corruption of the member goes limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of the whole body; and hasten to cut off,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the bite of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and their kinds.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is in the head of the tendon, then cut it, and do not give any space for it to come up as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut it at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that is the blow (i.e. death).
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy or medicine other than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do just the same when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then cut at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no remedy other than to kill the sick person.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or extracting the member is that you tie it from above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch out two servants one with each end of the thread downwards, and another servant with the other end of the thread upwards.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh that is between the two threads at one spatula-width wide, so that the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or extract it, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the extraction does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another lesion and abscess comes to the sick person.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if there is bleeding from the wound when you operate, then cauterize the area immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you place some restraining powder on it; then return to your medication until it is complete.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to him in the same way as he told me.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a burn that seemed like ash of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that burn came first to his two feet, so much so that it consumed the whole foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the burn, he had himself bandaged over the foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and a long time later the burn came back to both hands of him, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that would be irritating afterwards the cleansing of the body, and the burns could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I refused, because I had hope of recovering the substance;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the virtue of man was weak; and he completely lost hope, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he had himself bandaged over his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have only this tale to tell because it's what others do in times of need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At some time a pustule comes on the flesh and remains for so long that it forms a large cluster of boils.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they burst and open up, and the boils jump out, and the place is left empty, just like a vessel that has been emptied.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is also as delicate as a lightened cloth,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach all the way to the bone, nor all the way to the nerve, and diseases such as this are called "simple" illnesses.
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes right up to the bone in depth, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so delicate that you can cut all around it without harming it, even when it's as thin as a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it doesn't heal by its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not deep within,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and if the skin is thick with flesh, then clean it with a poultice in this way:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	examine to see if the boil on it is large and has a foul odor.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then treat it with Egyptian medicine made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take equal parts of lard, oil, and litharge, and put the mixture into a vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	so that the medicine is red and becomes just as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from it according to your need, and make it into water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use the poultice on the breast, and close the abscess.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay in for two hours, then remove it by pressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is clean and free of pus.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and any time it is poulticed with water from ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take the ashes of vine wood and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it cool and use the poultice, until you know that the breast is thoroughly clean.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the sick person cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or water from ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then treat it with a poultice of honey and water, or one part of litharge beaten in.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or treat it with a poultice of honey and sweet wine, because honey has the property to clean and purify.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound heal quickly.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and have faith that the breast is thoroughly clean,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then treat it with that which makes flesh grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take defrutum and make a plaster with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or treat it with some medicines and ointments, whose properties or recipes I have mentioned earlier for making ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the boil on the breast is small and the stick of the poultice cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it with a hot iron by a little bit, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or Basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then cut it back so that only one part of the poultice can enter it,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that emits pus is on top, then cut or move it so that it is lower.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the pus is deep inside, it should not leave any flesh to become inflamed.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut around the breast in the way that you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest point of the wound.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the pus is deep, it should not allow any flesh to become inflamed.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut around the breast in the way that you see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then arrange it so that the pus flows easily downward and nothing of the pus remains.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and spread a linen cloth over it so that it covers the entire breast.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut around the strongest part of the wound on the breast, one part larger than the first.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then spread soft ointment over another cloth according to the size of the wound.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on top of the breast wound to ease the pus, and do not remove the large cloth outside for a good while once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is over the breast wound, take it off often to remove the pus.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes out of the pus, whether it is venom or blood or enough or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there are any abscesses or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature of what is rising on top of the breast wound,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is healing well and approach the patient.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen the bandage in the morning or on the third day, and when you remove the dressing from the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change another cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast continues to discharge undigested pus for a good while, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom comes out after a long time, do not lose hope of recovery.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because the patient is approaching health. For there are people who gradually recover from flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested pus continues to come out of the breast after a good while, know that the breast has not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes too long to heal and is inflamed, then add medicines that are wet in substance but dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as defrutum, because it has a great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine to be used.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take defrutum and make a plaster with rose oil and the dregs of old wine, equal in quantity.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and do the same with honey that is cooked and thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defrutum is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then put the cloth on, and spread it on the breast, and administer it to no one who is an astrologer for a long time.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily which are also like flour of dates and centenary.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use them as simples or composites: grind them and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and the patient is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has taken hold deeply, and made an impression in the bone, or in the hard parts, or in the sinews.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so make a treatment for fistulae, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the lung.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pangarice is an abscess that arises under the lung of the palm of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps it arises in other parts.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and becomes old, it comes to be a large abscess.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and it runs and discharges pus as long as the root of the lung is running, and perhaps it spreads all over.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and it comes to corrosion just up to the bone, so that there is a stinking pain, and the lymph nodes of the throat are large, and the tongue has a foul color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the section on treatments, and the treatment does not bring any benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary to cut out all the remaining superfluity from the lung.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the lung is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the lung presses on the flesh and begins to putrefy and corrupt,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary to put a linen cloth under the lung that is pressing on the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up tightly at the top, and carefully and gently cut away that subtle and delicate flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out, and treat it with a poultice, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tongue corroding, then cut out a part of the palate just like it was said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it has become hardened and swollen, and causes great pain, then you must first lance it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the lung of the spatulum in a diagonal manner from above, cutting across.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not come near to the flesh that is under the lung, for the patient would feel too great a pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The tongue swells in some men's hands by chance, which is all flesh.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps it has such a shape that it has bones, and sometimes it has a lung.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them are born in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the bones of the tongue.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that arise in any part of the tongue do not mutter.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that arise at the joint of the tongue may be mute;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of one who is all flesh is slight, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatulum.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint is heavy to cure, and you must be careful when cutting him.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In he who is born in or at the end of the tongue, it is necessary to cut first the flesh around up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate thread for that, and treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come on the tongue in combination come from birth, or from a blow to the wound, or from burns of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut out that swelling, and then repair the tongue according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or moist cloths in rose oil, so that they do not swell again.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen, until the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a swelling comes to any part of his tongue with the palm, then cut out that swelling in such a way.
Des vils	Of the gums.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The gums are thick and swollen, full of melancholy superfluities that come in many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary to administer him a purging of gall, and then cleanse him with the sap of the basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to cut them, and then treat with a poultice the black sanicle;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you burn the gum, and treat it with a poultice all over.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is in this way: first heat the leg with hot water very strongly, so that the thick part of the bone is softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then take the leg of the sick person from above the knee down to the part under the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the gum in one place, or in two, or in three places, with a wide cut.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then loosen and treat with a poultice the black sanicle from one end to the other, as much as the patient's virtue can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it again, and command that he eats food that is gradually purging black gall.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the gums are full, and harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The removal of hair from the leg is in this way: shave the leg of the sick person, if it has much hair.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it becomes red and inflames the gums.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, then heat it over the fire, and then cut off the place of the gum as far back as the kneecap or in the part under the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then burn the skin with hot oil, and scrape off the gum from each part, until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters into the skin, it seems just like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then put a linen cloth under it, until it is lifted from the skin, and then dip it in hot oil lightly.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place above the three joints, then scrape off the skin on the gum until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then heat it with vinegar, just like you did before, and dip it in another hot oil, just like you did the first time.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another cut, or more if you need them, then heat it and cut into the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then treat and heat it up to the second cut, then pull it out from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw and lift it, then insert a needle into each thread tightly doubled.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and treat it, and insert it under a cloth, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut through, because if it cuts through, then you cannot draw or lift it, and it will harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have treated it all, then put a moist cloth of linen, in wine and rose oil, on the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the gums are contracted and twisted together, and not straight, as we have said before,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you cut them apart obliquely, but do not cut all the way through; and treat them as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron used to cut the gums is curved, and does not cut through, so that it cuts only the gum.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of thick curvature, because if it were thin, it would cut the bone, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of a civil gum.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This gum is purging in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in earth that has no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it arises in other parts than the legs, and those things happen from putrefaction that comes under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	like a serpent or worm, purging between the skin and flesh inside the body.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this gum are that it comes in the leg as a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the gum begins to come out, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the lump appears, it is necessary that you envelop it around a piece of linen from one and a half to two inches, and tie it up.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the linen attached to the leg, and every time it comes out again, envelop it in the linen and tie it up.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and envelop the remaining part, and do not cut through its root until it has come out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause abscess and putrefaction in that place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it is necessary to treat it little by little until the end, and leave nothing of it in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this gum, when treated, is as long as five or ten palms.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, from whom it issued as long as ten palms, and when you cut it, it makes a hole or a pit, and reaches right down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and the matter inside becomes empty, and administer to the place purging medicines for several days, then treat it as you would abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at any time to this vein is opened many veins, and indeed when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out with pus, and from which many veins burst; heal it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of oxen", because it happens many times to the oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all around the body, going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it feels very bad as it moves from limb to limb, until it comes out through the skin where it was going and bursts forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is engendered from the corruption of some humors, just as come worms and snakes and lice and ascarides in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts of its wickedness, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one can hardly tell what it was:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong thread tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cover on top of it and pull it out firmly, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you can't find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so then cauterize it with fire above, until it chars.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said before.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near to the head close to the eye, then bind a thread under it in the form of a loop, and pull it out firmly.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary for the sick person to use a cleansing of the body with dissolvent medicines for the corrupting humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of raw meats that engender corruption.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from windiness... (this seems to be a transition to a new topic)
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to an ill woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the upper arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and I, a little while after, saw it rise up as a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that place and fixes itself in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while after, it ran through all the body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that she was constantly twisting around the body, just as I had seen her doing.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this illness act in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often seen that the pain itself did move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but never in such a way as I saw it in the woman;
