et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that this was because the woman had a sick body and the veins were uncovered.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and so appeared the windiness, constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in this way to those who are healthy and have moist bodies and well-rounded veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see cure this illness, and the sick person feels that pain, if she shows it to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then bind a thread above and below hastily, and then pull it out firmly until the windiness constrained at that place bursts forth.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it yourselves,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat her with those who are skilled in breaking the windiness, such as pungent pills and serpent's pills and similar others.
Des saiettes	From arrows (this seems to be a transition to a new topic)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hair-tipped, and barbed.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two points, and those with feathers, and those with fragments (or "pieces").
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls in any member falls in two ways: either in the principal member it hurts,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you about afterwards is shown:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	it behooves you to beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes afterwards in various ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if that bad sign does not show itself to you, and the arrow is not deeply in place, then pull it out and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and the splinter is thrown forth which is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when you have blind spots and deafness and dizziness and redness in your eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is followed by a piercing pain in the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there comes out from the wound a moist white pus, resembling polyps, and also like the scab of an ulcer.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in too deeply.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the liver when it is struck by an arrow are that it feels like it was stuck in something hard and not empty, located near the left nipple, and there is also a sensation of hardness.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the liver swells like a boil, and there is a flow of black blood, and it comes with coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then have no doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that hits the stomach is that foam comes out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and gasps high and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the covering of the back, it is near the small ribs; and it emits great anguish and great pain and gasping, and the movement affects all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the abdomen and pus comes out through the intestine's route, then there is no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows away, and the sick person feels a very strong pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and forearms and wrists and legs and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it's not venomous, as I'll tell you happened to me, so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one of my friends, whose arrow hit him in the arm near the root of the nerve:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried and pulled it out from another side, under the ear fat, and he was healed without any injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that had hit him in the fatty part of the eye, under the eyelid.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was bent, and I could only grasp the tip near the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow's shaft without the ears; the boy was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears (i.e. had feathers).
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I grasped the barbs and pulled it out carefully until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from one man, who had it stuck in his stomach, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after passing thirty days, he didn't change his condition at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrowhead, and extracted it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see one man to whom an arrow has hit the back, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and he doesn't change his natural condition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor did it cause any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man to whom an arrow hit the face, and the wound was sewn up.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from one of the king's nobles, who had it stuck in his navel.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was entirely bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the care after it had been struck three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for the arrow with great subtlety and couldn't feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and aching under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the place a poultice attracting and digesting, so that the place wouldn't inflame.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the location of the arrow became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied another poultice for several days, and the wound healed again, and the sick person remained well for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	such that he felt the arrow one day inside his navel; and I told him so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied to the wound a corrosive caustic medicine for several days, until it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried and felt the tip of the arrow which had corroded at the place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that corrosive caustic medicine until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it completely healed around the edges in four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I ripped out the wound where I had inserted the pincers, and it came out from one side and the other, but couldn't come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop subtlety and trying in various ways with instruments, until I was able to get it out one day with well-made pincers.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to the form of what will come at the end of this chapter, as I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the sick person was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you can apply your care to what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters learn well and quickly from great small things, and from what is present and defective,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works and nine instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out from members where they are stuck unless according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they entered, or through another side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which comes out through the same side as it entered is an arrow entering a fleshy part and coming out only once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, then leave it alone until the flesh around is rotten and the exit is clear.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in a bone and cannot come out, then leave it alone for some days and move each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it comes out, and if not, pierce around with a very fine awl until the place around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the brains' vents,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and any of the accidents that I have said will happen to the sick person: do not pull it out at all, but leave it until it is equal in size after some days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes just up to the surface, that's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not come out until it reaches the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the sick person remains for some days without bad accidents, if he extracts it from pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out, then administer theriac around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is bent in the flesh of the body and cannot be seen, then search for it with all diligence.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in its way, then cut into it until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has feathers that hold it in place.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if cut away the flesh that is stuck on both sides where you can reach with your fingers.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the feathers of the arrow so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and do this carefully so that you don't break the arrow, but rather pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't get it out in one go, then leave it until the area around is rotten, and then pull it out, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding is contrary to what we have said about its treatment in this chapter, then apply that which we have said.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and take care not to cut the nerve and the vein, and think of how you can pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the sick person in the same form as he was when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because that is the greatest help it can be; and if you cannot, then put it in accordance with what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes out from another side, or it shows some indication of itself, or the skin is swollen in the place where you can see or feel it palpably:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut above until the pincers can take hold of it, and then pull it out; if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around so that it goes into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it alone again, and then resume the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is left, then insert the other end into its own shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft breaks and you need to administer binding, then insert one tool that is carved.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, then insert one tool with an entering point into it, to ease out the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, then it is fitting that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits the thigh or belly or bladder or ribcage and is close to it, and you can cut above, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, then pull it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers with which we pull out arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look at this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, small, and tiny, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the carved binding is also like a bird's feather.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to bind to the tip of the arrow, as shown by this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pincers for binding and piercing is such as this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins in the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which we bleed are thirty-one, of which sixteen are in the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	i.e., two plexuses that are behind the ears, which are called "the two herbaches".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in both visible temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are on the inner corners of the eyes, which are called "the aspirés".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead, and the vein that is at the head of the navel.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augerichs".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which we commonly bleed in each arm are five.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and common people call it "the vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median one is called "the vast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it "the vein of the heart", and the basilic vein is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and common people call it "the vein of the belly", and it is above the scrotum.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that of which we speak, which appears clearly above the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the scaphoid bone is the one that is between the thumb and the ring finger, and it has two joints;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three bones: one is below the knee joint of the left side.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second fibula which is at the ankle of the right side, and the third which is called "nasse", that is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three bones below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The joints of the bones that are behind the ears help with headaches and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the jointer, as I tell you, is that you elevate the head of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the arm or joints with a rough cloth; then wring the sick person's neck with a vice.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	so that the two joints behind the ears appear in two knots dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	ask him to bring it to your ear, and where you feel the pulse under your ear, press down.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the needle, and push it through the joint all the way to the bone, then lift your hand up all the way along the joint.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and clear out the skin and the joint well on both sides of the traveler, and let out blood as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and bind it, until it is sound.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The swelling of the two arteries which are in the two temples, is worth letting drain anciently,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and with an ointment of collyrium accustomed, and in the eyes a medicine of sharp tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the physician is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient stretches his neck so far that the two tendons appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels your elbow under your joint, and then signs with a nod.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the key up onto the tendon high at your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the tendon high, and cut it, just as you have done in the two other tendons, and make a cut of the blood according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then unloose the patient, and put your elbow over the tendon for an hour, then put on some cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then tie it firmly and let it be until it is healed; and now we have spoken of its cutting and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The physician of the vein of the forehead is worth just as much as the physician of the cephaleic for ancient diseases of the face, and for a migraine, and for a flush.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient stretches his neck in twisting, so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let the blood come out according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck and tie the vein so tightly that it is healed, and never once will you have to do it with a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable that the bandages are too tight; and the vein heals crookedly, because the bone is close, and perhaps breaks the bandages when they are stretched thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the temples is very helpful for them and for the itch, and for the flush, and for the hordeolum in the eye, and for diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their healing is that the patient stretches his neck in twisting from any cord, just as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then heal it, and let the healing of the transverse vein be one-third of the length of the bandage and one-third wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandages are thin, perhaps they will break; then make up with blood as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein of the neck is worth for ague, and for severe sweating, and for diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and flush that comes to the face, and especially when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the healing is that the patient stretches his neck, then stretches out his hand to your left with it.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a thin bandage long, and place it in the space between the two nostrils, near the lip.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep into it, and let the blood flow as much as you need, then tie it up for one night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the bandage:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The healing of the two gullets (or sinewy membranes) is helpful for the constriction of the anus, and for the beginning of ulcers, and for many diseases, and for impetigo, and for caries, and for herpetic lesions.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the healing is that the patient stretches his neck over one and then the other, just as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a stool.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the vein of length somewhat widely, then draw out blood temperately, or as much as need is.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then redo the other part in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and restrain the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and let him go until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of the lips:
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the veins of the upper lips is helpful for boils in the mouth, and for corruption of gums, and splits in the lips, and on the neck and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is to have the patient sit in front of you, and stretch his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn up the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left lip.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can know them by the fact that they are black, and because around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then cut one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you cut the thicker one from each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healing beneath the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins that are beneath the tongue is helpful after the healing of the cerebral vein, and it's for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the healer is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up his tongue, and looks beneath each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then cut one and the other, and do not go too deep, because beneath them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck that we commonly heal are healed in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a thick bandage to bind the whole thing strongly, or with an olive-shaped thin one, like the cuts we call "anasil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and their width and thickness are according to the size and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the thick bandage is well-known, and it's wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it needs to be used to open the thick veins full of clear blood that are apparent and contain a lot of blood and turmoil.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive-shaped bandage:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it's more delicate and pointed, and is for healing the thin veins where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and neck, and breast, and belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is fitting for the healer to cut carefully, and to beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding comes, then it is fitting to cauterize, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the bandage should not be applied, but rather cut in the manner of anasil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, then it is fitting that you tighten and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you take some of its juice out, or you cut into it in place of the basilic vein another vein in the arm: it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and then cut it with the bandage of anasil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know the place of the cut, then it is fitting to tighten the arm so that you touch the place as much as you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with incision and then bind the arm, and cut the vein of the bandage of anasil.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: then leave it alone.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then and put your finger on top lengthily, then take your finger away if the bleeding stops, for it has happened many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	then bind the arm and let it be, and do not move the patient until he is healed. And be on guard, and do not move him until he is well again.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it comes to you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, for the head will retreat; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a skin of fig tree, and burn it, and take one half and bind on well up to the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding stops, it's good; if not, then heal him with the powders that stop blood, as we have said.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of bleeding is not hurtful in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein in the middle helps it to draw blood from the head above and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cerebral veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is fitting for the healer to beware of the nerve that is beneath, and if he cuts too deeply, he will find the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the healing will be hurtful, and perhaps the patient cannot recover.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person because of its subtlety, then it is fitting that you cut the vein with the instrument anasil; and spare the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has veins between the two nerves, then burn them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the cerebral vein helps to draw blood from the head and helps those who are sick.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is fitting to heal with the olive-shaped bandage or the thick bandage, because it is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve nor artery beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is fitting to seek the lighter place, and do not hurt anything if we fail the first time, and start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the places swell in some people when we fail the first time, but it does not hurt them.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the healing is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know when it comes to healing, is that healing is most certain and effective when preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and in order to avoid and prevent illnesses from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the healing should be done in one of the three veins that are cut: to wit, the cerebral, the thoracic, and the basilic vein.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must heal in the beginning of spring and in autumn, after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must heal on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing that is administered for illnesses does not have a fixed time determined, but whenever there is need by day or night, at any hour and in all seasons.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it does not fit to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying more than four weeks until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should those who have passed 60 years be healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever manner it is, it is fitting that he purges his intestines with a light cathartic.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have many bad humors retained, so that the veins cannot draw out the superfluities which are noxious to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor can they be healed who are too fat with meat, or drunk, as long as it lasts, nor those who are dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and be wary of healing after severe colic, and vomiting, and bleeding from the stomach, and multiple times of frequent intercourse with a woman, and traveling, watching, and toiling, and all that is a great virtue, or by something of the arm or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then gently remove the humors, if the blood is thick, through meat and drink and medicines, if you have the power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then bathe or take a bath, as long as it doesn't harm him, to thin the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and treat the swelling around the navel for three days, just as we said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day of rest, and from work, and from lust, and from like things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be glad and joyful, and let the squire's hand be higher than that of the one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then stretch the ligament upwards slowly, for if it is too tight or slack, it cannot restore the blood;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub it with both hands, until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then wet the squire's flame with a spoonful of old oil, then put his thumb from his left hand on top of that swelling near the place to be healed;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the swelling does not burst and fall apart.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are swellings that burst open like strings when being healed, and of such kind as are full of wind.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	So that when one puts the flame on it, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the swelling, and thus is one of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it bursts the swelling, then the wound is too tight, for that reason it is necessary that the healer be wise in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the swelling bursts on the first time, it's good; and if not, then he starts again a little below or above that place where they were swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling is swollen and the patient fears it, then let him leave it for a day or two, and bind the arm not at all:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come good pustules on it; do not get into a bath, then start the healing again if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small or the blood runs thinly and you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you see, then put all the flame directly into that same wound itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and it will work a little quickly, thus before the swelling is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the swelling swollen, do not start healing again, and put a little linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body of the blood, and is more moist in that place than oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer linseed oil to each of the healings that you make for swellings, in order to staunch the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and it is also used for burns and blisters, when one puts it on the place; it thins the blood and separates when it becomes too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there come great pustules that have happened many times, exactly when it is not fully healed yet, or the opening of the swelling is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hasten and put on the place a moist sponge in warm water for a little while, and squeeze it out for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has stopped coming out of the swelling, and if there remains at the place after some days any blackness or greenish hue, then it does no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on some kind of aloes or myrrh dissolved in wine vinegar, mustard, or similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times has pustule and appearance to the healing of the boil: then put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put on any of what we have said, for perhaps it cuts the blood from the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each of the blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it ooze out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it come out until it becomes thinned; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for him who is full and has need of bloodletting to make the wound larger, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to heal him little by little, and he should be healed with a crosswise cut, not a piercing one.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is safe from bleeding and cutting of nerves, and is worth more than the healing by length or breadth.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for him who is in danger from the healing, it is necessary to give him a moist poultice with apple cider vinegar; if he is hot, treat the blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, make him a poultice before the healing with sweet syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cumin, and well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he smells bad during the healing, after the stoppage of bloody sweat, it is necessary that he inhale a broth made with meat and subtle, fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and follow the other things we have said in the chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the swelling.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to ease his arm, and mend it again, so it is necessary, when it is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed a little bit at a time, according to the quantity of his virtue continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wishes to ease his arm after the first bleeding, and it is very firm, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to be bled from another place, then he should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has much blood within the body that is already heated up, and makes fever come; so it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and to stretch the opening as wide as possible.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then that you stop all the bleeding conditions, and put your hand on the pulse when he bleeds, so that a clot does not come in place of the puncture.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the bleeder is neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see that the arm is loosened, and blood comes out the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	no, if it's curved, he should extend his arm hastily, for it would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave him alone until he bleeds the second time; or you can make a small prick with the tip of the flame, so that the blood which has coagulated comes out again easily.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on 1 pot of oil soaked in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swelled, then leave him alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to bleed again the second time, then let him bleed in the same spot, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the temporal vein because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding it is that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the vein is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then let him bleed now across, not too wide or too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the puncture be large, and let him bleed well close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's in winter, then don't put the hand back in hot water, for one puts less blood out in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding of this vein is safer from all other veins, for it has no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding of the temple vein of the right hand is worth to all illnesses of the liver, and this is how to do it:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and dip it into hot water, so that the vein is freed, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the skin is torn, and you close it with stitches from top to bottom, then nothing hurts;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all cut off from fat,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand into hot water, if the flesh is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn off as much blood as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and silk to solder it quickly, and do this with each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bloodletting from the left hand is worth for the disease of melancholy, and do all just as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	Bloodletting from the spleen is worth for all diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of humors, and diseases of the veins, and the thighs, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its bloodletting is that the sick person puts their foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it bleeds.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from there to the foot go many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Bloodletting there then does most good, from the largest vein, or at the ankle, which is most valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bloodlet above the foot, it will warn you of nerves that are beneath, and the bloodletting should cross also as in cutting; and the flames should be anesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood does not come out, then put the foot back in the water and let the vein be completely drained.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bloodletting fails the first time, then repeat it the second time above a little more, because the lesion is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt of nerves, as we have said, and do the same with the spleen of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The lesion of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the thigh, and its bloodletting is worth for pain in the backside, when it's for hot bleeding.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its bloodletting is that the sick person gets into a warm bath and rubs on the ankle with 4 turns in twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then let him bleed in all ways that you can, and crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is most valuable than cutting, because the lesion is salty, and it is very hardened in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it, then bloodlet the vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be wary of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and let it bleed as much as you see, and then untie the cord, and put on cotton and bind it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	A new topic! Let's continue.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Venesections are made from horns, or copper, or glass; and venesecting is done in two ways: either by piercing and attracting blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this venesecting which is done without piercing is in two ways: either it is red-hot or not hot at all;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and venesecting which is done by piercing and drawing out blood is done in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is at the top of the head and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on either side of the neck; and the venesection under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the venesection in both shoulders; and the venesection above the navel;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the venesections in both arms; and the venesections in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the venesections in both ankles; and venesecting does not treat great blood, but only small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it is not as effective, nor as good, as surgery of the vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not advisable that it be administered, nor at all hot or not hot, in any disease which comes from repletion, until the entire body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of illnesses or by custom it is necessary to venesect, let us administer each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in between and in every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are such people who, when they need to venesect, have headaches;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such people who find swelling and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness in themselves;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are such people who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and bleed from the gums;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such people who faint, and see things by themselves, blood, hurt, wounds, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it's in the middle of the month, let us command them to venesect three hours after lunch.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding of the menses helps to relieve the headache... that comes from themselves, and it is not advisable that this be done after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this venesecting takes the place of bleeding from the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not advisable that one who has a cold complexion or who is choleric uses this [venesecting], for it causes them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and because of that it is not advisable that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who cure themselves with this often become forgetful, and because of that it is advisable to place the venesecting a little lower down by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Venesecting in the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilar vein, and because of that it is worth it for the constriction of the abdomen.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for rupture of the channel of the womb, and at childbirth, and for repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be placed a little further down, because if it is too tightly closed, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The venesecting at the two corners of the neck is worth for headaches, and ophthalmia, and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of bleeding from the basilar vein. And let you command the surgeon to express his hand gently when applying, so that he does not compress the artery and comes out without any hemorrhage.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The venesecting below the chin is worth for diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it takes the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The venesecting of the armpits is worth for disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The venesecting of the sides is as good as the three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it drains blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh and lies near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The venesecting that is above the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below it. And let the venesecting be large and made of iron, so that it can draw well; and perhaps if it were subtle, it would break and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The venesectings of the legs are clearly curative, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for ancient pains in the reins, the bladder, and the kidneys, and they calm the ulcers; and they take the place of the two saphena veins and the two ankles. And moreover, they weaken the body after long use, and cause faintness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the venesecting is that you first put it on empty and then fill it with blood, quickly attach it to the body and move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then pierce, and reapply the venesectings, and take note of the condition of the body, for there are some who have thick flesh and clear pores: if so, you should only prick once, and make large and somewhat deep wounds, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it's necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out some blood little by little, one suffices once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we restart often; and if the blood is thick, we prick deeply, and the ends are such that the heart should be pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the venesectings with oil that is appetizing and dissolutive:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	such as olive oil, violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in youth, then of the oils of plantain, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or hawthorn oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person who is being cured has tender flesh and large pores, then it is not necessary to put any oil on them.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but rather it is necessary to wash with red water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, should get up with ashes, or mulberry water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities get up with old wine, or water of fig tree, or a decoction of hawthorn or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to be cured by venesecting before a bath or in the bath, but rather after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the venesecting.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he be warned when he should be venesected and when he has been venesected.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are being cured and are choleric, and the blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so that he takes cool things, such as green apples, endive, and lettuce with ashes, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and young boys, and beef broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and middle-aged wine that is between old and new, and young meat, and small birds and chickens.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will be venesected, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men some thyme or muscatel wine before the venesecting, or after, in order to comfort their main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and the blood should be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The venesectings that are not pierced are those that are put above the liver and above the spleen and gout and above the belly and the navel and the reins and the haunch, for these members do not bear to be pierced at all.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done in order to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as when we put them above the shoulders when there is a swelling, in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put venesectings above the belly and navel to diminish the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain when there is inflammation or an abscess, and it may by its attractive virtue remove the inflammation, or dry up the abscess from its place.
